   22→\n    23→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    24→// External Processing Filter\n    25→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    26→\n    27→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    28→\n    29→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    30→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    31→//\n    32→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    33→\n    34→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    35→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    36→//\n    37→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    39→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    40→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    41→//\n    42→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    43→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    44→// and how it should be processed.\n    45→//\n    46→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    47→//\n    48→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    49→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    50→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    51→//   sent asynchronously.\n    52→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    53→//\n    54→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    55→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    56→// processor must send a matching response.\n    57→//\n    58→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    59→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    60→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    61→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    62→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    63→//   to SEND.\n    64→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    65→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    66→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    67→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    68→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    69→//   request trailers.\n    70→//\n    71→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    72→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    73→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    74→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    75→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    76→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    77→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    78→//\n    79→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    80→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    81→//\n    82→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    83→//   on the content of the headers.\n    84→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    85→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    86→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    87→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    88→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    89→//\n    90→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    91→// server\n    92→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    93→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    94→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    95→//\n    96→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    97→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    98→// name.\n    99→//\n   100→// [#next-free-field: 18]\n   101→message ExternalProcessor {\n   102→  reserved 4;\n   103→\n   104→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   105→\n   106→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   107→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   108→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   109→\n   110→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   111→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   112→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   113→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   114→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   115→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   116→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   117→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   118→\n   119→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   120→  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n   121→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n   122→\n   123→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   124→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   125→  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n   126→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n   127→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   128→  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n   129→\n   130→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   131→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   132→  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n   133→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   134→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   135→  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n   136→\n   137→  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n   138→  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n   139→  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n   140→  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n   141→  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n   142→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   143→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   144→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   145→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   146→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   147→    gte {}\n   148→  }];\n   149→\n   150→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n   151→  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n   152→  string stat_prefix = 8;\n   153→\n   154→  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n   155→  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n   156→  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n   157→  // with the header prefix set via\n   158→  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n   159→  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n   160→  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n   161→  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. = \"proto3\";\n\npackage envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n\nimport \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n\nimport \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\noption java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\noption java_multiple_files = true;\noption go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\noption (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 18]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n    // definition for safe parsing.\n    repeated string typed = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n  // the external processing server.\n  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n}\n\n// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n//\n// This works as below:\n//\n//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n//   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\nmessage HeaderForwardingRules {\n  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n\n  // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n}\n\n// Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n// virtual host or cluster.\nmessage ExtProcPerRoute {\n  oneof override {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n    // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n    bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n\n    // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n  }\n}\n\n// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n// [#next-free-field: 8]\nmessage ExtProcOverrides {\n  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n  bool async_mode = 2;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n\n  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n  // config used. envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n     4→\n     5→import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n     6→import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n     7→import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n     8→import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n     9→import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n    10→\n    11→import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n    12→import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n    13→\n    14→import \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n    15→import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n    16→import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n    17→\n    18→option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n    19→option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n    20→option java_multiple_files = true;\n    21→option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n    22→option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n    23→\n    24→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    25→// External Processing Filter\n    26→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    27→\n    28→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    29→\n    30→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    31→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    32→//\n    33→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    34→\n    35→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    36→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    37→//\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    39→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    40→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    41→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    42→//\n    43→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    44→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    45→// and how it should be processed.\n    46→//\n    47→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    48→//\n    49→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    50→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    51→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    52→//   sent asynchronously.\n    53→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    54→//\n    55→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    56→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    57→// processor must send a matching response.\n    58→//\n    59→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    60→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    61→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    62→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    63→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    64→//   to SEND.\n    65→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    66→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    67→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    68→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    69→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    70→//   request trailers.\n    71→//\n    72→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    73→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    74→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    75→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    76→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    77→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    78→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    79→//\n    80→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    81→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    82→//\n    83→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    84→//   on the content of the headers.\n    85→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    86→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    87→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    88→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    89→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    90→//\n    91→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    92→// server\n    93→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    94→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    95→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    96→//\n    97→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    98→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    99→// name.\n   100→//\n   101→// [#next-free-field: 20]\n   102→message ExternalProcessor {\n   103→  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n   104→  // is received in response to request headers.\n   105→  enum RouteCacheAction {\n   106→    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n   107→    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   108→    // field is set in an external processor response.\n   109→    DEFAULT = 0;\n   110→\n   111→    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   112→    // the external processor response.\n   113→    CLEAR = 1;\n   114→\n   115→    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   116→    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n   117→    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n   118→    // to true.\n   119→    RETAIN = 2;\n   120→  }\n   121→\n   122→  reserved 4;\n   123→\n   124→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   125→\n   126→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   127→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   128→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   129→\n   130→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   131→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\noption java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\noption java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\noption java_multiple_files = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 20]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n    // field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n// 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\n//    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\n//    next chunk of the message body.\n// 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\n//    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\n//    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\n// 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\n//    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\n// 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n//    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n// 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n//    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n// 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\n//    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\n//    was configured to ignore errors.\n//\n// In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\n// using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\n// maintain state.\n\nservice ExternalProcessor {\n  // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\n  // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n  // protocol is described by the ProcessingRequest and ProcessingResponse\n  // messages below.\n  rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n  }\n}\n\n// This represents the different types of messages that Envoy can send\n// to an external processing server.\n// [#next-free-field: 11]\nmessage ProcessingRequest {\n  reserved 1;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Which\n  // ones are set for a particular HTTP request/response depend on the\n  // processing mode.\n  oneof request {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // Information about the HTTP request headers, as well as peer info and additional\n    // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n    // HeaderResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\n    HttpHeaders request_headers = 2;\n\n    // Information about the HTTP response headers, as well as peer info and additional\n    // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n    // HeaderResponse message or close the stream.\n    HttpHeaders response_headers = 3;\n\n    // A chunk of the HTTP request body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is true, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\n    HttpBody request_body = 4;\n\n    // A chunk of the HTTP response body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message or close the stream.\n    HttpBody response_body = 5;\n\n    // The HTTP trailers for the request path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\n    // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\n    //\n    // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\n    // the original downstream request has trailers.\n    HttpTrailers request_trailers = 6;\n\n    // The HTTP trailers for the response path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\n    // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\n    //\n    // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\n    // the original upstream response has trailers.\n    HttpTrailers response_trailers = 7;\n  }\n\n  // Dynamic metadata associated with the request.\n  config.core.v3.Metadata metadata_context = 8;\n\n  // The values of properties selected by the ``request_attributes``\n  // or ``response_attributes`` list in the configuration. Each entry\n  // in the list is populated from the standard\n  // :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>` supported across Envoy.\n  map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 9;\n\n  // Specify whether the filter that sent this request is running in :ref:`observability_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`\n  // and defaults to false.\n  //\n  // * A value of ``false`` indicates that the server must respond\n  //   to this message by either sending back a matching ProcessingResponse message,\n  //   or by closing the stream.\n  // * A value of ``true`` indicates that the server should not respond to this message, as any\n  //   responses will be ignored. However, it may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages\n  //   are needed.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 10;\n}\n\n// For every ProcessingRequest received by the server with the ``observability_mode`` field\n// set to false, the server must send back exactly one ProcessingResponse message.\n// [#next-free-field: 11]\nmessage ProcessingResponse {\n  oneof response {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\n    // ``request_headers`` field set.\n    HeadersResponse request_headers = 1;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\n    // ``response_headers`` field set.\n    HeadersResponse response_headers = 2;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``request_body`` field set.\n    BodyResponse request_body = 3;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``response_body`` field set.\n    BodyResponse response_body = 4;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``request_trailers`` field set.\n    TrailersResponse request_trailers = 5;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``response_trailers`` field set.\n    TrailersResponse response_trailers = 6;\n\n    // If specified, attempt to create a locally generated response, send it\n    // downstream, and stop processing additional filters and ignore any\n    // additional messages received from the remote server for this request or\n    // response. If a response has already started -- for example, if this\n    // message is sent response to a ``response_body`` message -- then\n    // this will either ship the reply directly to the downstream codec,\n    // or reset the stream.\n    ImmediateResponse immediate_response = 7;\n  }\n\n  // Optional metadata that will be emitted as dynamic metadata to be consumed by\n  // following filters. This metadata will be placed in the namespace(s) specified by the top-level\n  // field name(s) of the struct.\n  google.protobuf.Struct dynamic_metadata = 8;\n\n  // Override how parts of the HTTP request and response are processed\n  // for the duration of this particular request/response only. Servers\n  // may use this to intelligently control how requests are processed\n  // based on the headers and other metadata that they see.\n  // This field is only applicable when servers responding to the header requests.\n  // If it is set in the response to the body or trailer requests, it will be ignored by Envoy.\n  // It is also ignored by Envoy when the ext_proc filter config\n  // :ref:`allow_mode_override\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.allow_mode_override>`\n  // is set to false.\n  envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode mode_override = 9;\n\n  // When ext_proc server receives a request message, in case it needs more\n  // time to process the message, it sends back a ProcessingResponse message\n  // with a new timeout value. When Envoy receives this response message,\n  // it ignores other fields in the response, just stop the original timer,\n  // which has the timeout value specified in\n  // :ref:`message_timeout\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // and start a new timer with this ``override_message_timeout`` value and keep the\n  // Envoy ext_proc filter state machine intact.\n  // Has to be >= 1ms and <=\n  // :ref:`max_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.max_message_timeout>`\n  // Such message can be sent at most once in a particular Envoy ext_proc filter processing state.\n  // To enable this API, one has to set ``max_message_timeout`` to a number >= 1ms.\n  google.protobuf.Duration override_message_timeout = 10;\n}","numLines":200,"startLine":1,"totalLines":389}}}

If a response has already started -- for example, if this\n    // message is sent response to a ``response_body`` message -- then\n    // this will either ship the reply directly to the downstream codec,\n    // or reset the stream.\n    ImmediateResponse immediate_response = 7;\n  }\n\n  // Optional metadata that will be emitted as dynamic metadata to be consumed by\n  // following filters. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\nit to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\nand modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n\nThe protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01D5SnAcbQwvpb8YxuqXLuM2","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01PPNqxb3chgNnfiZXggJygM","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) Filter Migration Guide\n## v1.30.0 → v1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers the upgrade path for the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **v1.30.0 (April 2024)** to **v1.31.0 (July 2024)**.\n\nThe v1.31.0 release includes **one significant breaking change** to the route cache control mechanism, a **new feature** for deferred stream closure in observability mode, and **several implementation improvements**. The main impact for users is the deprecation of the `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field in favor of a more flexible `route_cache_action` enum field.\n\n**Migration Complexity:** Moderate - Most configurations will require a change to the route cache control field.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Control Refactoring\n\n**Impact Level:** 🔴 **HIGH** - All configurations using `disable_clear_route_cache` must be updated.\n\n#### What Changed\n\nThe route cache control mechanism has been refactored from a simple boolean flag to a more flexible enumeration type. This provides clearer semantics and better control over route cache behavior.\n\n**v1.30.0 - Original Field (DEPRECATED in v1.31.0):**\n```protobuf\n// In ExternalProcessor message\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 - New Fields (RECOMMENDED):**\n```protobuf\n// In ExternalProcessor message\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  DEFAULT = 0;  // Clear route cache based on response field\n  CLEAR = 1;    // Always clear route cache\n  RETAIN = 2;   // Never clear route cache\n}\n\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;  // Still supported but deprecated\n```\n\n#### Behavior Differences\n\n| Scenario | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 |\n|----------|---------|---------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | Clear route cache when `CommonResponse.clear_route_cache` is true | Use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | Never clear route cache, ignore `CommonResponse.clear_route_cache` | Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n| New option: Always clear | Not available | Use `route_cache_action: CLEAR` |\n\n#### Migration Path\n\n**Before (v1.30.0):**\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0):**\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n#### Validation Constraints\n\nIn v1.31.0, **only one of these fields can be set**:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache` (deprecated, boolean)\n- `route_cache_action` (recommended, enum)\n\nIf both are set, the configuration will fail with:\n```\nEnvoyException: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set at the same time\n```\n\nAdditionally, if `disable_clear_route_cache` is set to `true`, it will be automatically converted to `route_cache_action: RETAIN` during configuration initialization.\n\n#### Route Cache Behavior Semantics\n\n**DEFAULT (RouteCacheAction::DEFAULT = 0):**\n- Mirrors v1.30.0 default behavior\n- Clears route cache only when external processor response has `CommonResponse.clear_route_cache = true`\n- Most predictable and backward-compatible option\n\n**CLEAR (RouteCacheAction::CLEAR = 1):**\n- New in v1.31.0\n- Always clears the route cache when processing request headers\n- Useful when external processor frequently modifies request characteristics that affect routing\n- Incurs performance overhead due to route recalculation\n- Stat counter: `clear_route_cache_ignored` is not incremented\n\n**RETAIN (RouteCacheAction::RETAIN = 2):**\n- Equivalent to v1.30.0 `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n- Never clears the route cache, even if external processor sets `CommonResponse.clear_route_cache = true`\n- Useful for read-only external processors or when route cache invalidation is handled elsewhere\n- Stat counter: `clear_route_cache_disabled` increments when processor requests cache clearing\n\n#### Affected Code Locations\n\n- **Proto Definition:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto` (lines 101-120, 245-258)\n- **Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h` (FilterConfig class, new `routeCacheAction()` method)\n- **Validation Logic:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc` (FilterConfig constructor, lines ~214-220)\n- **Route Cache Processing:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc` (lines ~423-461)\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `disable_clear_route_cache` Boolean Field\n\n**Deprecation Status:** Deprecated in favor of `route_cache_action` enum\n\n**Timeline:**\n- v1.31.0: Still functional but marked for deprecation with UDPA migration annotation\n- Future: Will be removed in a later major version\n\n**Recommendation:** Migrate all configurations to use `route_cache_action` immediately to prepare for future removal.\n\n**Migration Path:**\n```python\n# Mapping from disable_clear_route_cache to route_cache_action\nif disable_clear_route_cache == true:\n    route_cache_action = RETAIN\nelif disable_clear_route_cache == false:\n    route_cache_action = DEFAULT  # or omit, as DEFAULT is implicit\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Enum\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**Purpose:** Provides explicit, semantic control over when route cache is cleared in response to external processor requests.\n\n**Field Details:**\n- **Proto Path:** `ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action` (field 18)\n- **Type:** `enum RouteCacheAction`\n- **Default:** Implicit DEFAULT (not set)\n- **Values:**\n  - `DEFAULT (0)`: Clear cache based on response field (backward compatible)\n  - `CLEAR (1)`: Always clear cache (new, unconditional clearing)\n  - `RETAIN (2)`: Never clear cache (was `disable_clear_route_cache: true`)\n\n**Use Cases:**\n\n| Use Case | Recommended Value |\n|----------|-------------------|\n| External processor may request cache clearing | DEFAULT |\n| External processor frequently modifies routing-sensitive headers | CLEAR |\n| External processor is read-only (e.g., logging) | RETAIN |\n| External processor handles routing logic separately | RETAIN |\n\n**Configuration Example:**\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear route cache for maximum freshness\n```\n\n### 2. Deferred Stream Closure Timeout\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**Purpose:** Controls how long gRPC streams remain open in observability mode after the HTTP stream closes, allowing for logging/telemetry collection without blocking request processing.\n\n**Field Details:**\n- **Proto Path:** `ExternalProcessor.deferred_close_timeout` (field 19)\n- **Type:** `google.protobuf.Duration`\n- **Default:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified\n- **Valid Range:** 0 - 3600 seconds\n- **Applies To:** Only used when `observability_mode: true`\n\n**Implementation Details:**\n- In observability mode, external processor streams don't send back responses\n- Envoy can process requests asynchronously without waiting for processor responses\n- Deferred closure allows external processor time to finish logging/telemetry before stream is terminated\n- Implemented via `DeferredDeletableStream` and `ThreadLocalStreamManager` classes\n\n**Configuration Example:**\n```yaml\nname: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: \"2s\"  # Give processor 2 seconds for telemetry\n```\n\n**When to Adjust:**\n\n| Scenario | Recommended Timeout |\n|----------|-------------------|\n| External processor logs to in-memory buffer | 500ms - 1s |\n| External processor sends to remote telemetry system | 2s - 5s |\n| External processor performs database writes | 5s - 10s |\n| Very high throughput, minimal processing | 100ms |\n\n**Performance Implications:**\n- Increasing timeout may increase memory usage (streams held longer)\n- Decreasing timeout may lose telemetry if processor doesn't complete in time\n- Default 5 seconds balances completeness vs. resource efficiency\n\n**Stat Tracking:**\n- New stats related to deferred stream closure are recorded internally\n- Visible in filter state under `ext_proc` namespace\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Required Changes for All Users\n\n1. **Audit existing configurations** for use of `disable_clear_route_cache`\n2. **Update proto files** if using generated code from v1.30.0\n3. **Modify Envoy configuration** files to use `route_cache_action`\n\n### Migration Checklist\n\n- [ ] Search all Envoy configurations for `disable_clear_route_cache` field\n- [ ] For each occurrence:\n  - [ ] If value is `true` → change to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n  - [ ] If value is `false` → change to `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (or remove, as DEFAULT is implicit)\n  - [ ] If not present → add `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` for clarity\n- [ ] Review external processor code for route cache assumptions\n- [ ] For observability_mode deployments, evaluate optimal `deferred_close_timeout`\n- [ ] Regenerate gRPC bindings from updated v1.31.0 proto files\n- [ ] Test configuration validation passes\n\n### Configuration Validation\n\n**Valid v1.31.0 Configuration:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    failure_mode_allow: true\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # ✓ Correct\n    observability_mode: false\n```\n\n**Invalid v1.31.0 Configuration:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true         # ✗ Deprecated\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN              # ✗ Can't set both\n```\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Clearing Logic\n\n**v1.30.0 Behavior:**\n```\nif CommonResponse.clear_route_cache == true:\n    if disable_clear_route_cache == false:\n        ClearRouteCache()\n    else:  // disable_clear_route_cache == true\n        IgnoreClearRequest()\nelse:\n    NoAction()\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 Behavior:**\n```\nmatch route_cache_action:\n    case DEFAULT:\n        if CommonResponse.clear_route_cache == true:\n            ClearRouteCache()\n    case CLEAR:\n        ClearRouteCache()  // Always\n    case RETAIN:\n        IgnoreClearRequest()  // Always, even if response requests it\n```\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Stream Lifecycle\n\n**New Behavior in v1.31.0:**\n- HTTP streams can complete and be destroyed while external processor streams remain open\n- External processor streams use `deferred_close_timeout` to stay alive for telemetry collection\n- Timer is set on filter destruction or explicit stream closure\n- Stream is forcefully closed when timer expires\n\n**Impact:**\n- External processor no longer blocks HTTP response delivery in observability mode\n- Telemetry collection is best-effort; not guaranteed to complete within timeout\n- Reduces latency for observability-mode deployments\n- May temporarily hold resources longer (for the timeout duration)\n\n### 3. Proto Imports\n\n**New Import in v1.31.0:**\n```protobuf\nimport \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n```\n\nThis annotation is used to track field migrations and provide guidance for backward compatibility handling.\n\n### 4. Message Changes\n\n**ExternalProcessor Message:**\n- `next-free-field` incremented from 18 to 20 (reserved for future extensions)\n- Two new fields added (18, 19)\n- One field moved with migration annotation (field 11)\n\n**No Changes to:**\n- `ProcessingMode` (still 7 fields)\n- `MetadataOptions` (still 2 nested fields)\n- `HeaderForwardingRules` (still 2 fields)\n- External processor service API (`service ExternalProcessor`)\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Update Envoy Binary and Dependencies\n\n```bash\n# Update to Envoy v1.31.0+\n# Rebuild any custom extensions or filters dependent on ext_proc\n# Regenerate control plane protobuf bindings\n\nprotoc --go_out=. \\\n       --go-grpc_out=. \\\n       envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto \\\n       envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto\n```\n\n### Step 2: Audit Current Configuration\n\n**Search for usage:**\n```bash\n# Find all ext_proc filter configurations\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /etc/envoy/\ngrep -r \"envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\" /etc/envoy/\n\n# Find all route-specific overrides\ngrep -r \"ExtProcPerRoute\" /etc/envoy/\ngrep -r \"ExtProcOverrides\" /etc/envoy/\n```\n\n### Step 3: Update Configuration Files\n\n**For each configuration file:**\n\n1. **Locate ext_proc filter definitions**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n```\n\n2. **Update route cache field**\n```yaml\n# OLD (v1.30.0):\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# NEW (v1.31.0):\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN  # Or DEFAULT, or CLEAR based on your needs\n```\n\n3. **For observability mode deployments, add:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: \"5s\"  # Adjust based on processor latency\n```\n\n### Step 4: Validate Configuration\n\n```bash\n# Syntax check\nenvoy --config-path /path/to/config.yaml --mode validate_only\n\n# Or with Envoy admin API after starting\ncurl http://localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.\"@type\" | contains(\"ExternalProcessor\"))'\n```\n\n**Expected output should show:**\n```json\n{\n  \"@type\": \"type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\",\n  \"grpc_service\": { ... },\n  \"route_cache_action\": \"DEFAULT\",\n  \"deferred_close_timeout\": \"5s\"\n}\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test External Processor Behavior\n\n**Test scenarios:**\n\n1. **Route Cache Behavior:**\n   ```bash\n   # Send request that triggers external processor route cache clear\n   curl -v http://localhost:10000/test-route-cache\n   # Verify in logs: route cache clearing behavior matches configured action\n   ```\n\n2. **Observability Mode (if enabled):**\n   ```bash\n   # Send requests with observability_mode: true\n   # Verify streams close after deferred_close_timeout\n   # Check that telemetry is collected even without responses\n   ```\n\n3. **Backward Compatibility:**\n   ```bash\n   # Test with old-style external processor that sets clear_route_cache field\n   # Verify behavior matches configured route_cache_action\n   ```\n\n### Step 6: Monitor and Validate\n\n**Key metrics to track:**\n```\nenvoy_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_ignored\nenvoy_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_disabled\nenvoy_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_upstream_ignored\n```\n\n- `clear_route_cache_ignored`: Increments when external processor requests cache clear with DEFAULT action\n- `clear_route_cache_disabled`: Increments when RETAIN action prevents cache clear\n- `clear_route_cache_upstream_ignored`: Increments for upstream filters (special handling)\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Unit Tests\n\nIf you maintain custom external processor implementations:\n\n```python\ndef the fields\n# Prefer route_cache_action:\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n# Don't include disable_clear_route_cache\n```\n\n**Issue: Route cache not clearing as expected**\n\n**Cause:** Configured action
